````text
## Workflow Orchestration
### 1. Plan Mode Default
- Enter plan mode for ANY non-trivial task (3+ steps or architectural decisions)
- If something goes sideways, STOP and re-plan immediately - don't keep pushing
- Use plan mode for verification steps, not just building
- Write detailed specs upfront to reduce ambiguity

### 2. Subagent Strategy
- Use subagents liberally to keep main context window clean 
- Offload research, exploration, and parallel analysis to subagents
- For complex problems, throw more compute at it via subagents
- One task per subagent for focused execution

### 3. Self-Improvement Loop 
- After ANY correction from the user: update `tasks/lessons.md` with the pattern
- Write rules for yourself that prevent the same mistake
- Ruthlessly iterate on these lessons until mistake rate drops
- Review lessons at session start for relevant project

### 4. Verification Before Done
- Never mark a task complete without proving it works
- Diff behavior between main and your changes when relevant
- Ask yourself: "Would a staff engineer approve this?"
- Run tests, check logs, demonstrate correctness

### 5. Demand Elegance (Balanced)
- For non-trivial changes: pause and ask "is there a more elegant way?"
- If a fix feels hacky: "Knowing everything I know now, implement the elegant solution"
- Skip this for simple, obvious fixes - don't over-engineer
- Challenge your own work before presenting it

### 6. Autonomous Bug Fixing
- When given a bug report: just fix it. Don't ask for hand-holding
- Point at logs, errors, failing tests - then resolve them
- Zero context switching required from the user
- Go fix failing CI tests without being told how

## Task Management
This project uses a **hybrid approach**: `tasks/todo.md` for AI context, GitHub Issues as the canonical tracker on the Harmony Project Board (course requirement).

1. **Plan First**: Write plan to `tasks/todo.md` with checkable items (local scratch pad for AI context)
2. **Identify the Issue**: If the task maps to an existing GitHub Issue, note the issue number at the top of `tasks/todo.md`
3. **Announce Start**: Post an opening comment to the issue — `gh issue comment <number> --body "..."` — describing what will be done
4. **Track Progress**: Mark items complete in `tasks/todo.md` as you go; post a comment to the issue at meaningful milestones (e.g., after a major step or when blocked)
5. **Explain Changes**: High-level summary at each step
6. **Document Results**: Add a review section to `tasks/todo.md` and post a final summary comment to the issue when complete
7. **Capture Lessons**: Update `tasks/lessons.md` after corrections. Post the new lessons learned as a comment to the issue.

### Issue Comment Format
Use this structure for issue comments to keep the audit trail readable:

```
**[AI Agent — <Step>]**

<What was done or decided>

<Any blockers, decisions, or next steps>
```

Example steps: `Starting`, `In Progress`, `Blocked`, `Complete`

## Core Principles
- **Simplicity First**: Make every change as simple as possible. Impact minimal code.
- **No Laziness**: Find root causes. No temporary fixes. Senior developer standards.
- **Minimal Impact**: Changes should only touch what's necessary. Avoid introducing bugs.
- **Lean Context Files**: Keep AGENTS.md and similar files to only non-obvious, non-discoverable essentials. Research shows context file bloat decreases task success rates and increases inference cost by 20%+ with 2–4 extra steps per task (Gloaguen et al., 2026).

#### Taken from https://x.com/mdancho84/status/2023738764841894352

Gloaguen, T., Mündler, N., Müller, M., Raychev, V., & Vechev, M. (2026, February 12). Evaluating AGENTS.MD: Are Repository-Level context Files helpful for coding agents? arXiv.org. https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.11988
````

```text
# PR Review Guidelines

When conducting PR Reviews, follow these guidelines:
1. **Prioritize Logic over Style:** Ensure the code is efficient, DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself), and logically sound.
2. **Security First:** Verify that the changes do not introduce vulnerabilities (e.g., lack of input validation, exposed secrets).
3. **Architectural Alignment:** If applicable, ensure the changes adhere strictly to the patterns defined in `@../docs/unified-backend-architecture.md`.
4. **Issue Completion:** If the PR is attached to an issue, verify that the code successfully satisfies every acceptance criteria of that issue.
5. **No Nitpicking:** Do not leave comments regarding stylistic choices, formatting, or subjective naming conventions unless they violate core project readability. Focus only on critical logic, performance, or architectural flaws.
6. **Avoid Repetition:** Do not repeat feedback that has already been stated in previous reviews on this PR.
7. **Iterative Reviews:** If this is not your first review on the PR:
    - First, check if the new commits have correctly addressed your previous review comments.
    - If a previous concern has been addressed, explicitly resolve the associated comment.
8. **Prevent CI Failures:** Analyze the code for obvious issues that would break the pipeline. Specifically check for syntax errors, missing imports/dependencies, unhandled exceptions, and logic that would clearly break existing tests.

**Execution Instruction**: Before providing your code feedback, output a markdown checklist of the 8 guidelines above. Mark each one as [x] if it passes or [ ] if it fails, and briefly explain why. Then, provide your single bundled review. Use inline subcomments within that single review for specific lines of codes. Do not post multiple standalone comments.
```

Output:

```text
import express, { NextFunction, Request, Response } from 'express';
import { createExpressMiddleware } from '@trpc/server/adapters/express';
import helmet from 'helmet';
import rateLimit from 'express-rate-limit';
import corsMiddleware, { CorsError } from './middleware/cors';
import { appRouter } from './trpc/router';
import { createContext } from './trpc/init';
import { authRouter } from './routes/auth.router';
import { publicRouter } from './routes/public.router';
import { seoRouter } from './routes/seo.router';
import { eventsRouter } from './routes/events.router';
import { attachmentRouter } from './routes/attachment.router';

const isE2E = process.env.NODE_ENV === 'e2e';

const loginLimiter = rateLimit({
  windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
  max: isE2E ? 1000 : 10,
  standardHeaders: true,
  legacyHeaders: false,
  message: { error: 'Too many login attempts. Please try again later.' },
});

const registerLimiter = rateLimit({
  windowMs: 60 * 60 * 1000, // 1 hour
  max: process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production' ? 5 : 1000,
  standardHeaders: true,
  legacyHeaders: false,
  message: { error: 'Too many registration attempts. Please try again later.' },
});

const refreshLimiter = rateLimit({
  windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
  max: isE2E ? 1000 : 30,
  standardHeaders: true,
  legacyHeaders: false,
  message: { error: 'Too many token refresh attempts. Please try again later.' },
});

export function createApp() {
  const app = express();

  app.use(helmet());
  app.use(corsMiddleware);
  app.use(express.json());

  app.get('/health', (_req, res) => {
    res.json({ status: 'ok', timestamp: new Date().toISOString() });
  });

  app.use(seoRouter);

  app.use('/api/auth/login', loginLimiter);
  app.use('/api/auth/register', registerLimiter);
  app.use('/api/auth/refresh', refreshLimiter);
  app.use('/api/auth', authRouter);

  app.use('/api/public', publicRouter);

  app.use('/api/events', eventsRouter);

  app.use('/api/attachments', attachmentRouter);

  app.use(
    '/trpc',
    createExpressMiddleware({
      router: appRouter,
      createContext,
      onError({ error }) {
        if (error.code === 'INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR') {
          console.error('tRPC error:', error);
        }
      },
    }),
  );

  app.use((_req: Request, res: Response) => {
    res.status(404).json({ error: 'Not found' });
  });

  app.use((err: Error, _req: Request, res: Response, _next: NextFunction) => {
    const isCorsError = err instanceof CorsError;
    const status = isCorsError ? 403 : 500;
    const message = isCorsError ? err.message : 'Internal server error';
    if (!isCorsError)
      console.error('Unhandled error:', process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production' ? err.message : err);
    res.status(status).json({ error: message });
  });

  return app;
}
```

#### Tool: exec_command

```sh
rtk read harmony-backend/src/index.ts
```

Output:

```text
import 'dotenv/config';
import { createApp } from './app';
import { cacheInvalidator } from './services/cacheInvalidator.service';

const PORT = Number(process.env.PORT) || 4000;

const app = createApp();

const server = app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`Harmony backend running on http://localhost:${PORT}`);
});

cacheInvalidator.start().catch((err) => console.error('[cacheInvalidator] start failed:', err));

let shuttingDown = false;
const shutdown = async () => {
  if (shuttingDown) return;
  shuttingDown = true;
  const timer = setTimeout(() => process.exit(1), 10_000);
  await new Promise<void>((resolve) => server.close(() => resolve()));
  await cacheInvalidator.stop();
  clearTimeout(timer);
  process.exit(0);
};

process.on('SIGTERM', shutdown);
process.on('SIGINT', shutdown);
```

```text
import request from 'supertest';
import { createApp } from '../src/app';
import type { Express } from 'express';

let app: Express;

beforeAll(() => {
  app = createApp();
});

describe('GET /health', () => {
  it('returns 200 with status ok', async () => {
    const res = await request(app).get('/health');
    expect(res.status).toBe(200);
    expect(res.body).toMatchObject({ status: 'ok' });
    expect(typeof res.body.timestamp).toBe('string');
  });
});

describe('GET /trpc/health', () => {
  it('returns 200 with tRPC result envelope', async () => {
    const res = await request(app).get('/trpc/health');
    expect(res.status).toBe(200);
    expect(res.body).toMatchObject({ result: { data: { status: 'ok' } } });
    expect(typeof res.body.result.data.timestamp).toBe('string');
  });
});

describe('404 handler', () => {
  it('returns 404 for unknown routes', async () => {
    const res = await request(app).get('/unknown-route');
    expect(res.status).toBe(404);
    expect(res.body).toMatchObject({ error: 'Not found' });
  });
});

describe('CORS', () => {
  it('returns 403 for disallowed origins', async () => {
    const res = await request(app)
      .get('/health')
      .set('Origin', 'https://evil.example.com');
    expect(res.status).toBe(403);
    expect(res.body).toMatchObject({ error: 'CORS: origin not allowed' });
  });

  it('allows requests from localhost:3000', async () => {
    const res = await request(app)
      .get('/health')
      .set('Origin', 'http://localhost:3000');
    expect(res.status).toBe(200);
  });
});
```

```text
     8	    ? 4000
     9	    : (() => {
    10	        const port = Number(rawPort);
    11	        if (!Number.isInteger(port) || port < 0 || port > 65535) {
    12	          throw new Error(`Invalid PORT environment variable: ${rawPort}`);
    13	        }
    14	        return port;
    15	      })();
    16	const HOST = '0.0.0.0';
    17	const DISPLAY_HOST = process.env.NODE_ENV === 'development' ? 'localhost' : HOST;
    18	
    19	const app = createApp();
    20	
    21	const server = app.listen(PORT, HOST, () => {
    22	  console.log(`Harmony backend listening at http://${DISPLAY_HOST}:${PORT} (bound to ${HOST}:${PORT})`);
    23	});
    24	
    25	cacheInvalidator.start().catch((err) => console.error('[cacheInvalidator] start failed:', err));
    26	
    27	let shuttingDown = false;
    28	const shutdown = async () => {
    29	  if (shuttingDown) return;
    30	  shuttingDown = true;
    31	  const timer = setTimeout(() => process.exit(1), 10_000);
    32	  await new Promise<void>((resolve) => server.close(() => resolve()));
    33	  await cacheInvalidator.stop();
    34	  clearTimeout(timer);
    35	  process.exit(0);
    36	};
    37	
    38	process.on('SIGTERM', shutdown);
    39	process.on('SIGINT', shutdown);
```

```text
    40	export function createApp() {
    41	  const app = express();
    42	
    43	  // Trust N proxy hops so req.ip and express-rate-limit can read
    44	  // X-Forwarded-For safely. Gated on TRUST_PROXY_HOPS so running the backend
    45	  // without a proxy in front (local dev, direct port exposure) doesn't let
    46	  // clients spoof XFF and poison rate-limit buckets. Set to `1` on Railway.
    47	  const trustProxyHopsEnv = process.env.TRUST_PROXY_HOPS;
    48	  if (trustProxyHopsEnv !== undefined && trustProxyHopsEnv.trim() === '') {
    49	    throw new Error(
    50	      `Invalid TRUST_PROXY_HOPS value "${trustProxyHopsEnv}". Expected a non-negative integer.`,
    51	    );
    52	  }
    53	  const trustProxyHops =
    54	    trustProxyHopsEnv === undefined ? 0 : Number(trustProxyHopsEnv);
    55	  if (!Number.isInteger(trustProxyHops) || trustProxyHops < 0) {
    56	    throw new Error(
    57	      `Invalid TRUST_PROXY_HOPS value "${trustProxyHopsEnv}". Expected a non-negative integer.`,
    58	    );
    59	  }
    60	  if (trustProxyHops > 0) {
    61	    app.set('trust proxy', trustProxyHops);
    62	  }
    63	
    64	  app.use(helmet());
    65	  // CORS must come before body parsers so error responses include CORS headers
    66	  app.use(corsMiddleware);
    67	  app.use(express.json());
    68	
    69	  // Health check (plain HTTP — no tRPC client required)
    70	  app.get('/health', (_req, res) => {
    71	    res.json({ status: 'ok', timestamp: new Date().toISOString() });
    72	  });
    73	
    74	  // SEO endpoints (robots.txt, sitemaps) — before auth so they're publicly accessible

    76

    78	  app.use('/api/auth/login', loginLimiter);
    79	  app.use('/api/auth/register', registerLimiter);
    80	  app.use('/api/auth/refresh', refreshLimiter);
```

- Time: 2026-04-11T14:56:44.398Z

- [ ] `1. Prioritize Logic over Style:` `PORT` validation still has a runtime gap: `process.env.PORT=''` passes through as `0`, so the server binds an ephemeral port instead of the configured one.
- [x] `2. Security First:` the earlier `trust proxy` spoofing risk is now gated behind `TRUST_PROXY_HOPS` and validated as a non-negative integer.
- [x] `3. Architectural Alignment:` this PR only changes process startup/network config and does not conflict with the backend architecture patterns.
- [x] `4. Issue Completion:` no linked issue or acceptance criteria were present on the PR, so there was nothing additional to verify here.
- [x] `5. No Nitpicking:` the review is limited to runtime behavior and deployment correctness, not style.
- [x] `6. Avoid Repetition:` I checked the existing review thread first; the remaining note below is distinct from the prior `TRUST_PROXY_HOPS` and logging comments.
- [x] `7. Iterative Reviews:` prior review comments appear addressed in the latest head commit, and I evaluated the current PR head rather than older revisions.
- [ ] `8. Prevent CI Failures:` this can still produce a deployment-time failure mode even if lint/tests/build pass, because a blank `PORT` results in listening on a random port.

I found 1 actionable issue on the current PR head: `harmony-backend/src/index.ts:5-15` still accepts a blank `PORT` and turns it into `0`, which makes Node choose an ephemeral port. That is a real deployment regression for a container/platform-managed port contract.

I did not run backend lint/tests on the PR head because the temporary review worktree did not have `node_modules` installed. Other than the `PORT` parsing gap, I did not find additional unaddressed problems in these two files.

### Turn 2: # Review findings: ## Finding 1

#### 👤 User Prompt

- Time: 2026-04-11T14:56:49.740Z

```text
# Review findings:

## Finding 1 (/tmp/harmony-pr314-yWRcEI/harmony-backend/src/index.ts:5-15) [added]
[P1] Blank PORT still slips through as an ephemeral bind

`rawPort === undefined` only rejects an unset variable. If the environment provides `PORT` as an empty or whitespace-only string, `Number(rawPort)` becomes `0`, passes the integer/range check, and `app.listen(0, ...)` binds a random ephemeral port. In a hosted environment that expects the process to listen on the provided `PORT`, the service becomes unreachable even though startup appears successful. This should be treated like the `TRUST_PROXY_HOPS` parsing path: reject blank input explicitly before numeric conversion, and likely reject `0` here unless ephemeral binding is intentionally supported.

## My request for Codex:
post it on the PR
```

#### 🤖 gpt-5.4 (medium)

- Time: 2026-04-11T14:57:35.750Z

Because the GitHub connector in this workspace rejected `file_comments` as plain strings.

The tool description I had exposed `file_comments` as `string[]`, but the connector validation error said:

`file_comments[0] [type]: Expected type ['object'], got str`

So the backend here is expecting structured inline-comment objects, not raw strings. That mismatch is likely coming from the workspace’s connector configuration or schema version, not from the PR itself.

Concretely:
- I sent a string entry like `"/path/to/file:5: comment..."`
- The connector wanted an object payload for each inline comment
- Since I don’t have the accepted object shape from this connector, the safe fallback was a normal review body with the exact file and line reference

If you want, I can try again using the lower-level GitHub PR review comment tools or inspect the connector behavior further.

This can mask misconfiguration in production (e.g., Railway) and make the process listen on an unexpected port. Consider explicitly validating <code class=\"notranslate\">process.env.PORT</code> when present (finite integer within 0–65535) and throwing on invalid values, while only defaulting to 4000 when <code class=\"notranslate\">PORT</code> is truly unset.</p>"},{"url":"https://github.com/CS485-Harmony/Harmony/pull/314#discussion_r3067918681","body":"`TRUST_PROXY_HOPS` parsing treats an empty string as `0` (`Number('') === 0`), which can silently disable `trust proxy` even though the env var is “set” (common in some deployment UIs). Behind a reverse proxy this would cause `req.ip`/rate-limiting to bucket all users under the proxy IP. Consider treating `''` (or whitespace-only) as invalid and throwing, similar to how other env parsing in the repo rejects malformed values.","user":{"login":"Copilot","name":"Copilot","email":null,"avatar_url":"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/in/946600?v=4","id":175728472},"id":3067918681,"pull_request_review_id":4093663072,"in_reply_to_id":null,"created_at":"2026-04-11T10:59:54Z","review":null,"side":"RIGHT","line":58,"start_line":47,"path":"harmony-backend/src/app.ts","body_html":"<p dir=\"auto\"><code class=\"notranslate\">TRUST_PROXY_HOPS</code> parsing treats an empty string as <code class=\"notranslate\">0</code> (<code class=\"notranslate\">Number('') === 0</code>), which can silently disable <code class=\"notranslate\">trust proxy</code> even though the env var is “set” (common in some deployment UIs). Behind a reverse proxy this would cause <code class=\"notranslate\">req.ip</code>/rate-limiting to bucket all users under the proxy IP. # PR Review Guidelines

```text
When conducting PR Reviews, follow these guidelines:
1. **Prioritize Logic over Style:** Ensure the code is efficient, DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself), and logically sound.
2. **Security First:** Verify that the changes do not introduce vulnerabilities (e.g., lack of input validation, exposed secrets).
3. **Architectural Alignment:** If applicable, ensure the changes adhere strictly to the patterns defined in `@../docs/unified-backend-architecture.md`.
4. **Issue Completion:** If the PR is attached to an issue, verify that the code successfully satisfies every acceptance criteria of that issue.
5. **No Nitpicking:** Do not leave comments regarding stylistic choices, formatting, or subjective naming conventions unless they violate core project readability. Focus only on critical logic, performance, or architectural flaws.
6. **Avoid Repetition:** Do not repeat feedback that has already been stated in previous reviews on this PR.
7. **Iterative Reviews:** If this is not your first review on the PR:
    - First, check if the new commits have correctly addressed your previous review comments.
    - If a previous concern has been addressed, explicitly resolve the associated comment.
8. **Prevent CI Failures:** Analyze the code for obvious issues that would break the pipeline. Specifically check for syntax errors, missing imports/dependencies, unhandled exceptions, and logic that would clearly break existing tests.

**Execution Instruction**: Before providing your code feedback, output a markdown checklist of the 8 guidelines above. Mark each one as [x] if it passes or [ ] if it fails, and briefly explain why. Then, provide your single bundled review. Use inline subcomments within that single review for specific lines of codes. Do not post multiple standalone comments.
```

### Turn 6: # Review findings: ## Finding 1

#### 👤 User Prompt

- Time: 2026-04-12T18:03:43.937Z

```text
# Review findings:

## Finding 1 (/tmp/harmony-pr314-yWRcEI/harmony-backend/src/index.ts:5-15) [added]
[P1] Blank PORT still slips through as an ephemeral bind

`rawPort === undefined` only rejects an unset variable. If the environment provides `PORT` as an empty or whitespace-only string, `Number(rawPort)` becomes `0`, passes the integer/range check, and `app.listen(0, ...)` binds a random ephemeral port. In a hosted environment that expects the process to listen on the provided `PORT`, the service becomes unreachable even though startup appears successful. This should be treated like the `TRUST_PROXY_HOPS` parsing path: reject blank input explicitly before numeric conversion, and likely reject `0` here unless ephemeral binding is intentionally supported.

## My request for Codex:
Review the PR again
```

Gated on TRUST_PROXY_HOPS so running the backend\n+  // without a proxy in front (local dev, direct port exposure) doesn't let\n+  // clients spoof XFF and poison rate-limit buckets.
```text
# PR Review Guidelines

When conducting PR Reviews, follow these guidelines:
1. **Prioritize Logic over Style:** Ensure the code is efficient, DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself), and logically sound.
2. **Security First:** Verify that the changes do not introduce vulnerabilities (e.g., lack of input validation, exposed secrets).
3. **Architectural Alignment:** If applicable, ensure the changes adhere strictly to the patterns defined in `@../docs/unified-backend-architecture.md`.
4. **Issue Completion:** If the PR is attached to an issue, verify that the code successfully satisfies every acceptance criteria of that issue.
5. **No Nitpicking:** Do not leave comments regarding stylistic choices, formatting, or subjective naming conventions unless they violate core project readability. Focus only on critical logic, performance, or architectural flaws.
6. **Avoid Repetition:** Do not repeat feedback that has already been stated in previous reviews on this PR.
7. **Iterative Reviews:** If this is not your first review on the PR:
    - First, check if the new commits have correctly addressed your previous review comments.
    - If a previous concern has been addressed, explicitly resolve the associated comment.
8. **Prevent CI Failures:** Analyze the code for obvious issues that would break the pipeline. Specifically check for syntax errors, missing imports/dependencies, unhandled exceptions, and logic that would clearly break existing tests.

**Execution Instruction**: Before providing your code feedback, output a markdown checklist of the 8 guidelines above. Mark each one as [x] if it passes or [ ] if it fails, and briefly explain why. Then, provide your single bundled review. Use inline subcomments within that single review for specific lines of codes. Do not post multiple standalone comments.
```
